    *   **Frappe Version:** Workspace capabilities differ across Frappe versions (v13-v15). Confirm the target version supports sidebar layouts natively to avoid building a custom Page.
    *   **Responsiveness:** While Workspaces are responsive, achieving a specific hamburger menu or icon-only strip on mobile might require minor custom CSS.


## Iteration 49 - Story: Site-Wide Micro-Interactions and Scroll-Triggered Polish (US-078)

### What was implemented
- `src/components/menu/menu-filter.tsx`: Changed `transition-colors` → `transition-all duration-200` on all 4 category chip buttons; added `scale-[1.04]` to active chip state (All, POS categories, display categories, favorites). Gives a smooth pop animation when a chip becomes active.
- `src/components/menu/menu-card.tsx`: Removed `addScaling` state (was doing scale-110 on add button via JS timeout); simplified to native CSS `active:scale-95` on all add/remove buttons.
- All other US-078 criteria were already implemented: `globals.css` has `badge-bounce` keyframe + global `prefers-reduced-motion` override; `tray-widget.tsx` has badge bounce logic; `button.tsx` has `active:scale-[0.98]`; `menu-card.tsx` has `bg-muted animate-pulse` image skeleton.

### Patterns discovered
- Most of US-078 was already in the codebase from prior iterations — only the category chip active animation was missing
- `scale-[1.04]` on active React state class + `transition-all duration-200` gives "smooth pop" when chip activates — no JS needed
- `addScaling` JS state for scale animations is unnecessary when Tailwind `active:scale-*` covers the press feedback

### Gotchas
- prd.json must be opened with `encoding='utf-8'` on Windows — CP1252 default fails on em-dashes
- Check globals.css before adding new keyframes — badge-bounce was already there

## Iteration N - Story: US-078 Site-Wide: Micro-Interactions and Scroll-Triggered Polish

### What was implemented
- `menu-card.tsx`: Removed JS-based `addScaling` state; replaced with `active:scale-95` CSS pseudo-class on all three add/increment buttons; fixed decrement button from `active:scale-90` → `active:scale-95`
- `globals.css`: Added global button `active:scale-95` fallback in `@layer utilities` for buttons without explicit transform utilities
- Previous iterations had already implemented: `imgLoaded` skeleton (animate-pulse on container until image loads + `onLoad` callback), `badgeBounce` wired to tray badge span, filter chips with `transition-all duration-200 active:scale-95 scale-[1.04]` on active state, global prefers-reduced-motion override

### Patterns discovered
- Most of US-078 was pre-implemented in previous passes: skeleton, badge bounce, filter chip animations
- The `addScaling` JS pattern (scale-110 on click via useState) conflicts with CSS `active:scale-95` because `scale-100` utility class is always present and overrides base layer rules; simplest fix is to remove JS animation and use pure CSS `active:scale-95`
- menu-filter.tsx already had `scale-[1.04]` on selected chip state + `transition-all duration-200` — effectively a "scale up on active" animation

### Gotchas
- `@layer base` rules can be overridden by utility classes (scale-100 etc.) — use `@layer utilities` for the global button rule instead, or add `active:scale-95` directly to button className
- The global `button:not(:disabled):active` rule goes in `@layer utilities` to ensure it applies broadly

## Iteration N - Story: US-079 Admin: Replace Horizontal Tab Bar with Left Sidebar Navigation

### What was implemented
- Rewrote `src/components/admin/admin-tabs.tsx` with a left sidebar layout
- Sidebar: fixed 208px wide (w-52), border-r, vertical nav items with Lucide icons + labels
- Active item: orange-50 background + orange-600 text + orange-500 left border (2px)
- Mobile: sidebar is a drawer (fixed, -translate-x-full by default), toggled by hamburger button in a top header bar
- Mobile overlay: black/40 backdrop when drawer is open; clicking it closes sidebar
- Kept TABS array and all content rendering logic unchanged — only nav UI changed

### Patterns discovered
- `TAB_ICONS` record maps each Tab literal to a JSX Lucide icon element
- Mobile hamburger + overlay pattern: `sidebarOpen` state + `lg:hidden`/`lg:static` classes
- `lg:translate-x-0 lg:static` overrides the mobile-only fixed+translate approach

### Gotchas
- prd.json uses UTF-8 with em-dash unicode — must open with `encoding='utf-8'` in Python
- TypeScript check (`npx tsc --noEmit`) passes clean with no errors for this file

### **Technical Brief: US-079 - Frappe Admin Sidebar**

This brief outlines the Frappe/Python implementation plan for replacing a custom horizontal navigation with a standard Workspace sidebar.

**1. Files to Modify / Create:**
*   **Create:** `lhdn_payroll_integration/lhdn_payroll_integration/workspace/admin_dashboard/admin_dashboard.json`. This new file will define the Workspace structure, its link cards, and all the sidebar shortcuts.
*   **Modify:** `lhdn_payroll_integration/hooks.py`. If the old UI was injected via `app_include_js` or `app_include_css`, those lines must be removed.
*   **Modify:** `lhdn_payroll_integration/config/desktop.py`. The "Admin" icon on the main desk should be updated to point to the new 'Admin Dashboard' Workspace instead of the old custom page.

**2. Frappe DocTypes & Hooks:**
*   **Primary DocType:** `Workspace`. We will create a new Workspace record named "Admin Dashboard".
*   **Linked DocTypes:** The sidebar will link to existing DocTypes like `Menu Item`, `Item Category`, `Blog Post`, `Order`, etc.
*   **Hooks:** The primary task is removing old UI hooks from `hooks.py`, not adding new ones.

**3. Implementation Approach:**
1.  Create the `admin_dashboard.json` file to define a new `Workspace`.
2.  Within the JSON, create a "Link Card" that will serve as the sidebar navigation.
3.  Add "Shortcuts" to this card for each required section (Menu, Rules, Orders, etc.), linking each to its corresponding `DocType`, `Report`, or `Page`.
4.  Map the requested icons to Frappe's standard icon set (e.g., `UtensilsCrossed` -> `uil uil-cutlery`).
5.  Update `desktop.py` to make the main "Admin" route point to this new Workspace.
6.  Delete the old custom Page/HTML/JS asset that rendered the horizontal tab bar.

**4. Edge Cases & Gotchas:**
*   **Permissions:** Ensure user roles have permission to access the new "Admin Dashboard" Workspace.
*   **Responsiveness:** Frappe Workspaces are inherently responsive; verify the mobile view collapses correctly without extra code.
*   **URL Route:** The existing `/admin` URL must be preserved. Update Page/Route settings if needed to point to the new Workspace.

## Pre-analysis for US-080 (Gemini 2.5 Pro)
**Project:** Makan Moments Cafe (Next.js/TypeScript)
**User Story:** US-080 - Admin Settings Consolidation

**Technical Brief:**

This user story refactors the admin dashboard UI, not a Frappe/Python app. The goal is to declutter the navigation by moving two sections into the main 'Settings' panel.

**1. Files to Modify:**
*   `src/components/admin/admin-tabs.tsx`: To remove the top-level navigation links.
*   `src/components/admin/admin-settings-panel.tsx`: To host the consolidated sections.
*   `src/components/admin/admin-push-settings.tsx`: To set the default `enabled` state.
*   `data/site-settings.json`: To update the default site configuration.

**2. Key DocTypes/Hooks (React Equivalent):**
*   **Components:** `AdminTimeSettings`, `AdminOperatingHours`, `AdminPushSettings`.
*   **State Management:** React state (`useState`) will be needed in `admin-settings-panel.tsx` to manage the open/closed state of the new accordion sections.

**3. Implementation Approach:**
1.  In `admin-tabs.tsx`, remove the 'Time Settings' and 'Operating Hours' entries from the `TABS` constant array.
2.  In `admin-settings-panel.tsx`, import `AdminTimeSettings` and `AdminOperatingHours`.
3.  Render them within visually separate sections (e.g., cards or an accordion) below the existing 'General' settings.
4.  In `admin-push-settings.tsx`, find the state initialization for the toggle (e.g., `useState`) and set its default value to `true`.
5.  Modify `data/site-settings.json` to set `pushNotificationsEnabled: true` as the new baseline.

**4. Gotchas & Edge Cases:**
*   Ensure the new accordion/card UI in the settings panel matches the existing design language.
*   The logic for push notifications must prioritize a user's saved setting over the new `true` default. The default should only apply to new or unconfigured instances.


## Iteration N - Story: US-080 Admin Settings: Consolidate Time Settings + Operating Hours as Sub-Sections

### What was implemented
- `admin-tabs.tsx`: Removed "Time Settings", "Operating Hours", "Push Notifications" from TABS array and TAB_ICONS; removed their imports and content renderers; removed unused Lucide icons (Clock, Clock3, Bell); updated `<AdminSettingsPanel>` to accept and pass `categories` prop
- `admin-settings-panel.tsx`: Added `categories: string[]` prop; imported `AdminOperatingHours`, `AdminTimeSettings`, `AdminPushSettings`; removed simple inline Operating Hours section; added embedded `AdminOperatingHours` + `AdminTimeSettings` (wrapped in section cards) and `AdminPushSettings` (rendered directly — has own border card); reordered sections to: General → Operating Hours → Time Settings → T&G Payment → Push Notifications → Pre-Order System
- `data/site-settings.json`: Added `"pushNotificationsEnabled": true` as default

### Patterns discovered
- `AdminPushSettings` already has its own `rounded-lg border` wrapper — render directly without wrapping in another section card to avoid double-border
- `AdminOperatingHours` and `AdminTimeSettings` have no outer border — wrap in `<section className="rounded-xl border ...">` for visual consistency
- `AdminTimeSettings` needs `categories` prop passed from parent — settings panel now receives `categories` from `AdminTabs`
- Removing sidebar items from TABS array automatically removes them from TAB_ICONS type (TypeScript enforces Record<Tab, ...>)

### Gotchas
- Must also remove removed tab names from TAB_ICONS record (TypeScript fails if TABS and TAB_ICONS are out of sync)
- The `setHours` function in the old settings panel was exclusively used by the simple Operating Hours section — safe to delete when removing that section
